Music therapy—a type of expressive arts therapy that uses music to improve and maintain the physical, psychological, and social well-being of individuals—involves a broad range of activities, such as listening to music, singing, and playing a musical instrument.
Music therapy can both assess and enhance cognitive, social, emotional, and motor functioning, and studies have shown positive results among individuals who have intellectual or physical difficulties, brain injuries, or Alzheimer's.

    z=qn;
end

17/05/23, 15:44 - Himral: a) To determine the peak phase deviation, we need to find the maximum value of the modulation term in the angle modulated signal. In this case, the modulation term is 4 sin(2000πt). The peak phase deviation (Δφ) is equal to the maximum value of this modulation term.

The maximum value of sin(2000πt) is 1, so the peak phase deviation is:

Δφ = 4 × 1 = 4 radians

b) The peak frequency deviation (Δf) can be calculated using the relationship between phase deviation and frequency deviation in angle modulation. For small angle deviations, the relationship is given by:

Δf = (Δφ / 2π) × fm

Where Δf is the peak frequency deviation, Δφ is the peak phase deviation, and fm is the maximum frequency of the modulation signal.

In this case, the maximum frequency of the modulation signal is 2000 Hz, so we can calculate the peak frequency deviation as:

Δf = (4 radians / 2π) × 2000 Hz
     = (2/π) × 2000 Hz
     ≈ 1273.24 Hz

Therefore, the peak frequency deviation is approximately 1273.24 Hz.

c) This is an FM (Frequency Modulation) signal. In frequency modulation, the instantaneous frequency of the carrier wave varies proportionally with the instantaneous amplitude of the modulating signal. In the given signal, the modulation term 4 sin(2000πt) is a sinusoidal waveform that modulates the instantaneous frequency of the carrier signal. Hence, it exhibits the characteristics of frequency modulation and is classified as an FM signal.

05/08/23, 22:22 - Ishita 💕: Various types of multiplexing can be used to share the listed resources:

1. CPU: Time multiplexing 

2. Memory: Both time and space multiplexing

3. Disk: time multiplexing,

4. Network card: Time multiplexing

5. Printer: Printers can use both time and space multiplexing.

6. Keyboard: time multiplexing,

7. Display: time multiplexing,

Real-life scenarios:

1. Space Multiplexing: In a computer data center, multiple servers are hosted within a rack. To save physical space and cost, a KVM (Keyboard, Video, Mouse) switch is used. It allows a single set of keyboard, mouse, and monitor to be shared among all the servers. This is an example of space multiplexing as the same peripherals are used for multiple servers.

2. Time Multiplexing: In cable television broadcasting, different channels share the same transmission medium (coaxial cable or fiber). Each channel is allocated a specific time slot for transmission, and they take turns transmitting their content. This is an example of time multiplexing, commonly known as Time-Division Multiplexing (TDM) in telecommunications.

22/09/23, 09:26 - Vidhi 💕: #include <stdio.h>
#include <pthread.h>

// Structure to hold employee information
struct EmployeeInfo {
    char name[50];
    int hallNo;
    int employeeID;
    char branch[50];
};

// Function that prints employee information
void *printEmployeeInfo(void *arg) {
    struct EmployeeInfo *info = (struct EmployeeInfo *)arg;
    printf("Name: %s\n", info->name);
    printf("Hall No.: %d\n", info->hallNo);
    printf("Employee ID: %d\n", info->employeeID);
    printf("Branch: %s\n", info->branch);
    pthread_exit(NULL);
}

int main() {
    pthread_t thread1, thread2;
    int rc1, rc2;
    struct EmployeeInfo emp1, emp2;

    // Employee 1 information
    strcpy(emp1.name, "John Doe");
    emp1.hallNo = 101;
    emp1.employeeID = 1001;
    strcpy(emp1.branch, "Engineering");

    // Employee 2 information
    strcpy(emp2.name, "Jane Smith");
    emp2.hallNo = 102;
    emp2.employeeID = 1002;
    strcpy(emp2.branch, "Sales");

    // Create thread 1
    rc1 = pthread_create(&thread1, NULL, printEmployeeInfo, (void *)&emp1);
    if (rc1) {
        printf("ERROR: return code from pthread_create() is %d\n", rc1);
        return 1;
    }

    // Create thread 2
    rc2 = pthread_create(&thread2, NULL, printEmployeeInfo, (void *)&emp2);
    if (rc2) {
        printf("ERROR: return code from pthread_create() is %d\n", rc2);
        return 1;
    }

    // Wait for threads to complete
    pthread_join(thread1, NULL);
    pthread_join(thread2, NULL);

    return 0;
}

22/09/23, 09:26 - Vidhi 💕: #include <stdio.h>
#include <pthread.h>

#define NUM_THREADS 5
  
pthread_mutex_t mutex = PTHREAD_MUTEX_INITIALIZER;

 
void *
printHello (void *threadID)
{
  
long tid = (long) threadID;
  
 
    // Lock the mutex to ensure exclusive printing
    pthread_mutex_lock (&mutex);
  
printf ("Hello World!Thread #%ld!\n", tid);
  
    // Unlock the mutex to allow other threads to print
    pthread_mutex_unlock (&mutex);
  
 
pthread_exit (NULL);

} 
 
int

main ()
{
  
pthread_t threads[NUM_THREADS];
  
int rc;
  
long t;
  
 
for (t = 0; t < NUM_THREADS; t++)
    {
      
printf ("Creating thread %ld\n", t);
      
rc = pthread_create (&threads[t], NULL, printHello, (void *) t);
      
if (rc)
	{
	  
printf ("ERROR: return code from pthread_create() is %d\n", rc);
	  
return 1;
	
}
    
}
  
 
    // Wait for all threads to finish
    for (t = 0; t < NUM_THREADS; t++)
    {
      
pthread_join (threads[t], NULL);
    
}
  
 
printf ("All threads have completed.\n");
  
 
pthread_exit (NULL);

}
